<rate>5< /rate>< review>
I live in a rural area where one would not expect to get anything except satellite or maybe a poor cellular data connection.  DigitalPath able to find line of sight to a local tower on the top of one of my trees on which they installed an antenna. I work at home and use the internet intensively, mainly Remote Desktop, VoiP/Conferencing and Email.  High bandwidth is not a requirement, but low latency and stable uptime are a big deal. My first few weeks of service i experienced regular dropouts and loss of service which would cause painful work interruptions.  I worked with their tech support to troubleshoot the issue and they determined the cause was likely with the antenna/tree equipment.  The climbers came back out and after a second trip up the tree, my connection has been stable with zero drop outs for over 2 weeks now.

I have been on the phone several times for various reasons, each time the wait time was reasonable (with audio prompts telling you how people are in the queue before you).  In addition they update their initial tech-support greeting with today's date and a summary of known outages.

This morning I woke to a service outage, I called the support line and learned right off the bat that there was an outage in my area and included an estimate time of service restoration. No need to even speak to a tech.  I headed into town and worked at a coffee shop and after returning home I am writing this up using my DigitalPath connection.

These guys are top notch at communication and the service is just what I need for working in the tech world from the middle of a forest. A+++

I am on the 10 Mbps / 2 Mbps plan which is delivered as advertised.

One other thing to note.  If you plan on relying on this kind of service the way I do, you should consider that this kind of technology is heavily reliant on atmospheric conditions.  Plan to have a backup if you have any mission critical tasks that depend on the internet.  If you have line of sight and these guys can't make it work, you probably need to explore other options.< /review>

Once you hit your data limit in a billing cycle, your speeds will be reduced to 10% of the normal speed. We typically have 2 options in a situation like this: First, we are happy to troubleshoot more with you on what could be using up all of your data. From experience, we have seen the following things use a lot of data very quickly: a) customers with one or more wireless router(s) that are not password protected or neighbors having your wireless password and using your data without you knowing it; b) 4K or HD video streaming on one or more devices. The more devices used at the same time, the faster you eat up your data. This is usually the main cause of large data consumption for our customers; c) watching satellite TV ON DEMAND movies or shows, because they actually use your internet connection to stream the movies; d) video game downloads or updates. A second option if it turns out this is actual usage after investigating more, is to look at upgrading to our 1,000GB plan for another $25/month that would better support your current data usage so that you do not have your speeds slowed to 10% of normal half way through your billing cycle like has been happening to you the last few months. < review>
Using for over 4 years and still inconsistent! Sometimes speeds are good and other times absolutely horrible. It seems about every year Digital Path is upgrading equipment or dealing with some kind of power outage. Realistically they are probably overselling their available bandwidth and as a result customers including myself have slow speeds (evening & weekends) and at times no connection. In the years I've been with Digital Path I've called over 40 times. If I could move to another provider, I would, but nothing as of yet in my small town. That may change next year, but I'll have to wait and see. Let's be clear this company could go three stars or more- but their advertised speeds are just not correct (most of the time they trickle to a crawl) and over the years no one is able to clearly explain what is really going on. Honesty would go much further then excuses for their wish washy answers. Note- I've talked with a few of their installers over the years and they've basically said the same thing - if you can get DSL or something else go for it Are they better than Frontier- in my opinion yes. Is the service better than dial-up; yes. Is it better than satellite, well that depends on your location.<//review>

*EDIT*
They recently upgraded to the new generation of equipment. My speed and data cap increased substantially and the price went down too. I am changing my rating to 5 stars.

Overall:
Best Internet available for my needs at this time, however I will switch to cable the second it is available(which may never happen).

Reliability:
Very reliable service, i have only had a handful of outages in 2+ years, much more reliable than Comcast in the Sacramento area.

Speed:
Highest available to me in rural cottonwood without switching to high-latency Satellite service. 10Mbps/2Mbps. Faster speeds available in town.

Bandwith:
Huge data caps (500GB) available.

Price:
$130.95 for this tier(10Mbps w/400gb cap). Outrageously high compared to cable providers where they are available.< /Review>

It's kind of just a 'Screw you stop calling us.' Rather than being helpful. It's been well over a year and their quality has steadily been going down hill. The odd thing is though, is that when you sign up for the first few months everything works perfectly, but after that good luck checking your emails.

If you have ANY other options explore them first. For me this is my only option unfortunately. Steer clear.</Text>

<review>The USPS is not paid for by tax dollars any more. Getting your mail is a privilege not a right. The USPS is a company run by human beings, human beings make mistakes, no one is perfect. The vast majority of USPS employees want your experience to be positive, carriers are not intentionally trying to damage or slow down your mail. Postal carriers are breaking their backs in the heat, cold and rain hauling your heavy packages up and down stairs and hills every single day. USPS carriers work Saturdays and Sundays to make sure your packages are delivered in a timely manner. Carriers frequently walk 5 to 15 miles a day. Mail carriers put their lives on the line every day to make sure you get your mail delivered. A simple "thank you" can go a long way sometimes. Blowing up on an online forum or review site because you didn't get one  package delivered on time is completely unfair and inconsiderate of the massive amount of work that the USPS does every single day for their millions of customers.

The vast majority of complaints I am seeing on here may be caused by errors on the customers side.

#1 Make sure the address is 100% accurate. If you don't include the apartment number, suite number or complete and accurate address (North, South, East, West, etc.) it will probably be held at the office for a few days while the carriers try to locate the correct address or sent back to sender if they are not able to locate you. Sometimes packages end up on the wrong route and will be delayed. The USPS does not guarantee delivery time on any of their mail except Express mail. If you are sending something that absolutely must be there at a certain time send it Express mail.

#2 Check your mailboxes regularly. Your mail will be held at the post office for a few days and then sent back to the sender if your mailbox is full. Mail carriers cut their hands, jam their fingers and sprain wrists trying to put mail in mailboxes that have not been checked properly by the customer.

#3 If you move or go on vacation talk to your mail person, go online or go to the office and let the USPS know. Your mail may be held at the post office for a few days and sent back to sender if you do not let the USPS know ahead of time.

#4 If you order an extremely over sized package do not be surprised if you have to go pick it up yourself at the post office. The mail carriers vehicles are the size of a small pickup truck bed. Large packages can take up to 40% of the truck space and keep the carrier from loading the rest of their days mail safely and securely.<//review><gmap_id>0x80c295153a67f589:0x8c662e64f1baf35e</gmap_id>< rating>

<rating>2< /rating>< review>
My family and I moved into Chesapeak Commons in 2008. We wanted something affordable and small. The place provided a decently size living room and somewhat smaller than normal kitchen, but it's something that should be expected when moving into an apartment.

After living there for 10 years already, we very slowly disliked the location, but since we had no money, we had to live with the negatives...but for 10 years.

The first thing is MAINTENANCE. It ridiculous on the timeframe they gave you for the maintenance people to come and fix a certain item in your place. We had to fix our washer and dryer, oven (that was never fixed, which I'll explain why soon), replace our microwave, fix our sink and food dispenser, and lastly a major leak from the washer that spread  throughout the whole living room. Now all of these problems did not happen in a short period. It happened over time. What my we didn't like was that the maintenance people took too long to come by and FIX the problems that was happening. Their time frame to fix something was between 9am to 5pm and a specific day/date would be given. That is a long time between those the time frame. Someone would have to be home to ensure the door is unlocked and ready to ask questions just in case. BUT 80% of the time, THEY DO NOT SHOW UP. They did not show up AND did not give a notice that they would not show up. IF THEY DID SHOW UP, they would look at the problem, THEN schedule another day to fix it, AND BY GOD if we are lucky if they stick between the time frame. WE HATED IT EVERYTIME they missed the time frame. Of course we know there is other units that need to be fixed, but GIVE THE TENANTS A SPECIFIC TIME FRAME ON A CERTAIN DATE THAT THEY ARE DEFINITELY READY TO COME BY. We called the office, but there excuse was that it was up to the maintenance if they would be done or not with their previous fix.

Next the neighborhood and the area is not a safe area. We have seen people move in and move out for a long time. Their reasons are on their own, but what we have noticed was the following: multiple cars pass by playing loud hip hop/pop/rnb or just ghetto music late at night, someone stole a car part under our vehicle at night, someone BURNED a marijuana plant above our unit that caused the fire department to come by to assess the situation, we found 7 (yes we counted) people sneaking around the master bedroom window and their reason was that they were peeing, and lastly the individuals that move in are not THAT nice to other tenants.

They made multiple upgrades to the apartment, which is a positive thing about Chesapeake Commons. Every year since 2008, they increased our monthly pay for a 2 bedroom, 1 bathroom unit. So, make sure you're reading your lease agreement if you're planning on renewing it. They assigned parking for the units, upgraded other people's equipment, improved the decoration for the clubhouse for parties, and made sure the grass is always green, which was not always trimmed before the upgrades and new policy changes.

The agents seem nice at first, but what I think is very intimidating about them is that they seem to NOT care about the tenants needs. One individual, though, who is nice and reasonable is Laurie. Before we finally moved out in 2017, she understood our situation of how short in money we were, so she helped us out definitely. I would recommend seeing her first and foremost about anything. EVERYBODY ELSE seem like they are about to find something wrong OR trying to find something wrong in your apartment and try to charge you. They don't call you or anything but instead stick a paper on your door, so it makes you WORRY and always LOOK over your shoulder. IT keeps you not safe from any ACCIDENTAL or a small mistake you did. THEY WILL CHARGE YOU NO MATTER WHAT. IF MAINTENANCE COMES BY, THEY WILL TELL THE AGENTS OF ANYTHING THAT SEEMS OUT OF THE ORDINARY.

So DO YOUR RESEARCH OF THE PLACE. AND IF YOU COULD,  DECIDE ANOTHER PLACE IF POSSIBLE. THIS PLACE SHOULD BE YOUR LAST RESORT. Please and thank you.<//review>
